{\\n167: public:\\n168:   /**\\n169:    * Return a sorted vector of registered factory names.\\n170:    */\\n171:   static std::vector<absl::string_view> registeredNames(bool include_disabled = false) {\\n172:     std::vector<absl::string_view> ret;\\n173: \\n174:     ret.reserve(factories().size());\\n175: \\n176:     for (const auto& [factory_name, factory] : factories()) {\\n177:       if \\n495: /**\\n496:  * Factory registration template. Enables users to register a particular implementation factory with\\n497:  * the FactoryRegistry by instantiating this templated class with the specific factory class and the\\n498:  * general Base class to which that factory conforms.\\n499:  *\\n500:  * Because factories are generally registered once and live for the length of the program, the\\n501:  * standard use of this class is static instantiation within a linked implementation's translation\\n502:  * unit. For an example of a typical use case, @see NamedNetworkFilterConfigFactory.\\n503:  *\\n504:  * Example registration: REGISTER_FACTORY(SpecificFactory, BaseFactory);\\n505:  *                       LEGACY_REGISTER_FACTORY(SpecificFactory, BaseFactory, \\\"deprecated_name\\\");\\n506:  */\\n507: template <class T, class Base> class RegisterFactory {\\n508: public:\\n509:   /**\\n510:    * Constructor that registers an instance of the factory with the FactoryRegistry.\\n511:    */\\n512:   RegisterFactory() {\\n513:     ASSERT(!instance_.name().empty());\\n514:     FactoryRegistry<Base>::registerFactory(instance_, instance_.name());\\n515: \\n516:     // Also register this factory with its category.\\n517:     //\\n518:     // Each time a factory registers, the registry will attempt to\\n519:     // register its category here. This means that we have to ignore\\n520:     // multiple attempts to register the same category and can't detect\\n521:     // duplicate categories.\\n522:     if (!FactoryCategoryRegistry::isRegistered(instance_.category())) {\\n523:       FactoryCategoryRegistry::registerCategory(instance_.category(),\\n524:                                                 new FactoryRegistryProxyImpl<Base>());\\n525:     }\\n526:   }\\n527: \\n528:   /**\\n529:    * Constructor that registers an instance of the factory with the FactoryRegistry along with\\n530:    * deprecated names.\\n531:    */\\n532:   explicit RegisterFactory(std::initializer_list<absl::string_view> deprecated_names) {\\n533:     if (!instance_.name().empty()) {\\n534:       FactoryRegistry<Base>::registerFactory(instance_, instance_.name());\\n535:     } else {\\n536:       ASSERT(deprecated_names.size() != 0,\\n537:              \\\"Attempted to register a factory without a name or deprecated name\\\");\\n538:     }\\n539: \\n540:     for (auto deprecated_name : deprecated_names) {\\n541:       ASSERT(!deprecated_name.empty());\\n542: FactoryCategoryRegistry::registerCategory(instance_.category(),\\n547:                                                 new FactoryRegistryProxyImpl<Base>());\\n548:     }\\n549:   }\\n550: \\n551: RegisterFactory(uint32_t major, uint32_t minor, uint32_t patch,\\n564:                   const std::map<std::string, std::string>& version_metadata,\\n565: \\n495: /**\\n496:  * Factory registration template. Enables users to register a particular implementation factory with\\n497:  * the FactoryRegistry by instantiating this templated class with the specific factory class and the\\n498:  * general Base class to which that factory conforms.\\n499:  *\\n500:  * Because factories are generally registered once and live for the length of the program, the\\n501:  * standard use of this class is static instantiation within a linked implementation's translation\\n502:  * unit. (!FactoryCategoryRegistry::isRegistered(instance_.category())) {\\n523:       FactoryCategoryRegistry::registerCategory(instance_.category(),\\n524:                                                 new FactoryRegistryProxyImpl<Base>());\\n525:     }\\n526:   }\\n527: \\n528:   /**\\n529:    * Constructor that registers an instance of the factory with the FactoryRegistry along with\\n530:    * deprecated names.\\n531:    */\\n532:   explicit RegisterFactory(std::initializer_list<absl::string_view> deprecated_names) {\\n533:     if (!instance_.name().empty()) {\\n534:       FactoryRegistry<Base>::registerFactory(instance_, instance_.name());\\n535:     } else {\\n536:       ASSERT(deprecated_names.size() != 0,\\n537:              \\\"Attempted to register a factory FactoryCategoryRegistry::registerCategory(instance_.category(),\\n547:                                                 new FactoryRegistryProxyImpl<Base>());\\n548:     }\\n549:   }\\n550: \\n551: Envoy Extension Registry and Factory Architecture\\n\\nThe Envoy C++ codebase implements a sophisticated extension registry pattern for dynamic discovery and instantiation of extension implementations. This pattern is central to Envoy's plugin architecture.\\n\\n### Core Registry System\\n\\n**Registry Template Class (envoy/registry/registry.h:166)**\\n\\nThe `FactoryRegistry<Base>` template class is the core of the registry system. It maintains a static hash map of factory instances keyed by name using `factories()` (line 190), and provides factory lookup methods:\\n- `getFactory(name)` (line 293): Looks up factory by string name\\n- `getFactoryByType(type)` (line 302): Looks up factory by protobuf configuration type\\n- `registeredNames()` (line 171): Returns sorted vector of all registered factory names\\n- `registerFactory()` (line 230, 247): Registers factory instances with optional versioning\\n\\n**Factory Registration (envoy/registry/registry.h:507-597)**\\n\\nThe `RegisterFactory<T, Base>` template class is a CRTP-style registration mechanism. When instantiated (typically as a static variable), its constructor automatically registers a static instance of factory T with the FactoryRegistry<Base>. There are two variants:\\n\\n1. Static instantiation mode (ENVOY_STATIC_EXTENSION_REGISTRATION): Factories are registered via static global variables created by the REGISTER_FACTORY macro (line 622-626)\\n2. Dynamic registration mode: Factory registration is triggered via `forceRegister*()` functions (line 641-645) that create the RegisterFactory instances on-demand\\n\\n**Registration Macros (envoy/registry/registry.h:618-665)**\\n\\nThree key macros provide the public API:\\n\\n1. `REGISTER_FACTORY(FACTORY, BASE)` - Registers a factory class with a base class\\n2. `LEGACY_REGISTER_FACTORY(FACTORY, BASE, DEPRECATED_NAME)` - Registers with deprecated name support\\n3. `DECLARE_FACTORY(FACTORY)` - Declares the forceRegister function for linking in static archives\\n\\nThese macros expand to either static RegisterFactory instances or function definitions depending on the build configuration.\\n\\n### Factory Base Classes\\n\\n**Core Interfaces (envoy/config/typed_config.h)**\\n\\nAll factories derive from `UntypedFactory` (line 14), which defines the factory interface:\\n- `name()`: Returns the factory's name (reversed DNS recommended)\\n- `category()`: Returns the factory category for automatic registration\\n- `configTypes()`: Returns protobuf message types handled by the factory\\n\\nThe `TypedFactory` (line 41) subclass adds:\\n- `createEmptyConfigProto()`: Creates an empty configuration protobuf message\\n\\n**Filter Factory Hierarchies (envoy/server/filter_config.h)**\\n\\nThe filter config module defines specialized factory base classes:\\n- `ListenerFilterConfigFactoryBase`: Base for listener filters\\n- `NamedListenerFilterConfigFactory`: Listener filter factories\\n- `NamedUdpListenerFilterConfigFactory`: UDP listener filter factories  \\n- `NamedQuicListenerFilterConfigFactory`: QUIC listener filter factories\\n- `NamedNetworkFilterConfigFactory`: Downstream network filter factories\\n- `NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory`: HTTP filter factories (line 273)\\n- `HttpFilterConfigFactoryBase`: Base class for HTTP filters\\n\\nEach defines a `category()` method returning the extension category (e.g., \\\"envoy.filters.http\\\").\\n\\n### Factory Lookup and Usage\\n\\n**Factory Lookup Utilities (source/common/config/utility.h)**\\n\\nThe `Utility` class (line 67) provides factory lookup methods:\\n\\n1. `getFactoryByName<Factory>(name)` (line 240): Looks up factory by name, returns nullptr if not found\\n2. `getFactory<Factory>(message)` (line 253): Looks up by type first, falls back to name if not found\\n3. `getFactoryByType<Factory>(typed_config)` (line 327): Looks up factory by protobuf configuration type URL\\n4. `getAndCheckFactory<Factory>(message)` (line 293): Lookup with error checking, throws if not found\\n\\nThese utilities internally call `Registry::FactoryRegistry<Factory>::getFactory()` and related methods.\\n\\n### Factory Category Registry\\n\\n**Category Registration (envoy/registry/registry.h:104-146)**\\n\\nThe `FactoryCategoryRegistry` maintains a map of factory categories. When a factory registers via RegisterFactory, it automatically registers its category if not already present (line 522-525). This enables:\\n- Discovering all available factory categories\\n- Querying factories by category\\n- Disabling factories by category name\\n\\n### Static Initialization and Self-Registration\\n\\n**Static Extension Registration Pattern**\\n\\nExtensions self-register at static initialization time through several mechanisms:\\n\\n1. **Global Variable Instantiation**: In static registration mode, each extension defines a static RegisterFactory instance.
